  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5c3811f3-081b-47bd-a14f-39997fc2b308'
      });

<div class='spoiler'>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Pauline wouldn't have known anything about Tom's wife since she had no contact with him once she fled home (at least, she didn't know she was having c<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Pauline wouldn't have known anything about Tom's wife since she had no contact with him once she fled home (at least, she didn't know she was having contact with him). Clearly he was manipulative and controlling and had abused his wife into a state of coercion, using her as an accomplice.<br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3432872897" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3432872897?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3432872897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7534528131700522294"><b>Undone is another horrific, yet intriguing installment in the Will Trent series.<br/><br/>This book is the most sickening and gruesome of the series that I have read so far. Focused on women who have been abducted and assaulted in ways I didn't even know were possible, it was nauseating to read. </b><br/><br/>Undone brings Sara Linton into the fold. Faith, who is battling some personal issues, takes an immediate dislike to the doctor, while Will experiences quite the opposite. <b>Angie makes one appearance, and in my opin</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7534528131700522294" style="display:none"><b>Undone is another horrific, yet intriguing installment in the Will Trent series.<br /><br />This book is the most sickening and gruesome of the series that I have read so far. Focused on women who have been abducted and assaulted in ways I didn't even know were possible, it was nauseating to read. </b><br /><br />Undone brings Sara Linton into the fold. Faith, who is battling some personal issues, takes an immediate dislike to the doctor, while Will experiences quite the opposite. <b>Angie makes one appearance, and in my opinion, this was one too many. </b><br /><br />I found the beginning slow, and I am not sure if it was due to the nature of the crimes, or something else that was going on, but I struggled to connect for the first half of the book. However, as Will and Faith moved deeper into solving the case and the mystery grew deeper, so did my interest. <br /><br /> By then end, I couldn’t put this book down. I didn’t love seeing Sara, but at the same time (since I have read book 8), I am well aware of what's to come. <b>Betty is still my favorite character, lol! <b><br /><br />I am addicted to this series and ready for book 4 NOW!</b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7534528131700522294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_383965761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383965761" />
    <a title="Karin Slaughter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10901279-karin-slaughter"><img alt="Karin Slaughter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565730663p2/10901279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383965761?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin Slaughter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin Slaughter" href="/user/show/10901279-karin-slaughter">Karin Slaughter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10901279-karin-slaughter?shelf=will-trent-series">will-trent-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383965761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18203615407947083131">First, people should know that in the UK and elsewhere, this book is titled Genesis, which was the original title I chose. (In the US, there was another book called Genesis--sci-fi--that was publishing around mine and they didn't want confusion). I chose the title Genesis because this was really a restart for Sara Linton. She's in a new city, she's completely changed her life, she's still recovering from the horrible events in Beyond Reach (weirdly, called Skin Privilege in the UK and other terr</span>
  <span id="freeText18203615407947083131" style="display:none">First, people should know that in the UK and elsewhere, this book is titled Genesis, which was the original title I chose. (In the US, there was another book called Genesis--sci-fi--that was publishing around mine and they didn't want confusion). I chose the title Genesis because this was really a restart for Sara Linton. She's in a new city, she's completely changed her life, she's still recovering from the horrible events in Beyond Reach (weirdly, called Skin Privilege in the UK and other territories...) I felt very keenly that I needed for readers to mourn alongside Sara, but I couldn't let it be so raw that she couldn't actually function, so I set the story a few years after Beyond Reach. So, we hear about what she went though, but we also see that there is a light peeking over the horizon.<br /><br />This is also the first book where Sara meets Will Trent, which is something I had planned way back when I wrote Triptych. I see that book as well as Fractured (the only Will books without Sara) as Will's preparation for meeting Sara. He's starting to shake off Angie, he gets partnered with Faith Mitchell (whom I consider a grumpy Watson to Will's Holmes in that she makes him explain the things that are running around in his head and pulls him out of his shell), his relationship with Amanda is becoming more open...so, he's kind of learning how to be the sort of man that Sara would be interested in. And readers, too!<br /><br />SPOILER!<br /><br />I also write about a widow on Cop Town (June 2014) which I didn't realize until I had finished the book. What's this with me and widows? I guess I find it interesting, because how do you go on when you lose the love of your life? It doesn't seem possible, but people have to do it every day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18203615407947083131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2072732512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072732512" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2072732512?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099509752" href="/book/show/7789435-genesis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=trigger-warning">trigger-warning</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2072732512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5556938571219426431"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501222601ra/23432827.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>TW - the so-called "hero" is a rapist, and everyone hates women because why the fuck not</b><br/><br/>Alright. It's way too late for me to write a 10,000+ review, but <b>I'm so fucking disgusted that I have to talk about it or I'll never sleep.</b> Let's go to the point, okay? <br/><br/>So. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7789435.Genesis__Will_Trent___3_' title='Genesis (Will Trent, #3) by Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Genesis</a>. Or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5764902.Undone__Will_Trent___3_' title='Undone (Will Trent, #3) by Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Undone</a>, whatever it's named. I'm so angry I can't see straight. So, so angry because I've been enjoying this series so far, including the beginning of this one, I've made excuses for the rampant sexism pouring through every pag</span>
  <span id="freeText5556938571219426431" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501222601ra/23432827.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>TW - the so-called "hero" is a rapist, and everyone hates women because why the fuck not</b><br><br>Alright. It's way too late for me to write a 10,000+ review, but <b>I'm so fucking disgusted that I have to talk about it or I'll never sleep.</b> Let's go to the point, okay? <br><br>So. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7789435.Genesis__Will_Trent___3_" title="Genesis (Will Trent, #3) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Genesis</a>. Or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5764902.Undone__Will_Trent___3_" title="Undone (Will Trent, #3) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Undone</a>, whatever it's named. I'm so angry I can't see straight. So, so angry because I've been enjoying this series so far, including the beginning of this one, I've made excuses for the rampant sexism pouring through every page, and now I'm feeling so sick, I want to unread this book. <br><br>The thing is, <b>there's a tiny limit between picturing realistic, flawed characters and making me loathe every one of them.</b> God, I had hopes for Will!<br><br>However, <b>that was before I knew that he was a fucking rapist.</b><br><br>Yes, you heard me. You won't change my mind with the "Angie is a manipulative bitch" narrative, because you know what? Of course she is, I hate the woman, <b>but that's very dangerous to draw lines when it comes to rape. There's NO woman on earth who deserves to be raped. I don't CARE if the book is telling us that oh, actually, she enjoyed it. SHE SAID STOP. SHE FUCKING SAID STOP.</b> I will NOT feel sorry for Will. Was she on the verge of forcing his hand? YES. Would she have been an awful human being if she had managed to do it? YES. But why would Will be let off the hook? There's no such thing as "eyes for an eye, and teeth for a tooth" as far as I'm concerned, because then why would I care for him?? Why would I root for him? <b>He's accountable for his actions all the same, and as much as I liked the guy, now he's like a itch I want to scratch. GO AWAY.</b> <br><br>Things go like this : she's trying to force his hand and manipulate him, he (understandably!!) tells her to leave. She doesn't. He then starts pushing her. She fights back. She pushes him on the floor. He holds on and pulls her down with him. He uses his force to keep her under him. And then : <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He grabbed both her hands in one of his, <b>squeezing them together so she couldn't fight him.</b> Without even thinking, he reached down and <b>ripped away</b> her underwear. Her nails dug into the back of his hand as he slid his fingers inside her.<br>'Asshole," she hissed, but she was so wet Will could barely feel his fingers moving in and out. (...)<br><b>'Stop it,'</b> she demanded, but she was moving against his hand, tensing with each stroke. He unzipped his pants and pushed himself inside her. <b>She tried to tighten against him, but he pushed harder, forcing her to open up.</b>"</i>
</blockquote><br>In the end, she enjoys it and has an orgasm. I don't care. The fact that she's wet, that she has pleasure, doesn't change a thing, because <b>we really don't need more scenes like these in medias, scenes in which no means yes.</b> What the <i>hell.</i> Do I really have to explain why? WHY THE FUCK DO WE LET PEOPLE IMPLY THAT THE BOUNDARIES BETWEEN ANGER AND DESIRE ARE SO THIN? They aren't. Why are we excusing this kind of behavior? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501222601ra/23432826.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>We need to stop dismissing this as 'rough sex' : that's not rough sex, that's rape.</b><br><br>And THEN the guy dares think, <b>
  <i>"He was so sick of this, so sick of the way Angie drove him to extremes"</i>
</b> Oh, no no no, you don't. You don't get to feel sorry for yourself and find excuses. Angie is bad news, but she's also been abused in the past. This doesn't excuse her behavior, but it doesn't excuse Will either because guess what, jerk, you are always responsible for your own actions. Again, I hate Angie, but no. No you don't. Even if she enjoys it after, it doesn't change a thing. <b>Will is still this guy who forces himself on her and who doesn't stop when she asks him to and I don't want to read about that fucking guy.</b><br><br>Yes, she wanted to have sex with him <i>before their argument</i>. <b>But that's not how consent works. Consent can be withdrawn at ANY moment. </b> That's sex 101 for crying out loud. <br><br>The issue is never addressed after because Will never acknowledges that what he did wasn't right. The narration implies that it's all Angie's fault, and I'm not here for that. Oh no I'm not.<br><br>Secondly, what is IT with Faith's internalized misogyny? Amanda's? <b>Is there ONE person in that entire book who doesn't act like a sexist pig?</b> Actually, yes, there's Will. <i>Right.</i> Too bad he's our resident's rapist. I said before that I understood the need to picture a realistic world. But again, you can portray flawed characters without creating a world entirely filled with complete assholes. You can use your narrative to help dismantling stereotypes. <br><br>It's called talent. <br><br>Here it was sometimes done, but way too rarely for me. <b><u>This is rape culture at its finest, where everyone including women think of women as petty bitches.</u> The whole thing felt dehumanizing and that was very lazy storytelling.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501222601ra/23432828.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally : the victims. <b>The way anorexia was handled felt very offensive to me,</b> and I'm not sure why the parallel between their bitchy attitude and their eating disorder was drawn so tightly. I understand that it revolved around the killer's reasons for choosing them, but it still did not sit well with me. <br><br>I just can't believe no one called Will out on his rape. I'm just - I'm feeling sick and I want to cry.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202531669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3256893778949202617">Karen Slaughter doesn't make violence pretty; these are not cozy mysteries to wile away the hours. I am not preaching against those types of mysteries, because I like them too. She does public service by not dressing up sexual psychopaths. These men are sick and what they do to women is repugnant and nightmare-enducing, that said she also knows people and that's what brings me back to her novels again and again. The violence is tough to read, but the fine people who try to help by solving these </span>
  <span id="freeText3256893778949202617" style="display:none">Karen Slaughter doesn't make violence pretty; these are not cozy mysteries to wile away the hours. I am not preaching against those types of mysteries, because I like them too. She does public service by not dressing up sexual psychopaths. These men are sick and what they do to women is repugnant and nightmare-enducing, that said she also knows people and that's what brings me back to her novels again and again. The violence is tough to read, but the fine people who try to help by solving these horrific crimes, though damaged themselves, are worthy of our attention.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3256893778949202617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1700930273" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1700930273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2516030241640609414">Undone by Karin Slaughter is a 2009 Delacorte Press publication.<br/><br/><br/>This third book in the Will Trent series creates a link with the Grant County series by introducing Sara Linton to the series. <br/><br/>Sara is from Grant County, but has relocated to Atlanta following the death of her husband. She meets Faith and Will at the hospital when Faith has a fainting spell, but soon finds herself embroiled in the case Will and Faith are working on. <br/> <br/><br/>Several women who have been tortured or are missing has Faith and </span>
  <span id="freeText2516030241640609414" style="display:none">Undone by Karin Slaughter is a 2009 Delacorte Press publication.<br /><br /><br />This third book in the Will Trent series creates a link with the Grant County series by introducing Sara Linton to the series. <br /><br />Sara is from Grant County, but has relocated to Atlanta following the death of her husband. She meets Faith and Will at the hospital when Faith has a fainting spell, but soon finds herself embroiled in the case Will and Faith are working on. <br /> <br /><br />Several women who have been tortured or are missing has Faith and Will working overtime, while dealing with their own personal demons and various disabilities. A lot happens in this installment and like the first two in the series, this one had me on the edge of seat the entire time I was reading it. But, now that I have settled into the series a little more, I find myself becoming quite involved with Will and Faith’s personal lives, as well as the case at hand. <br /><br />I love complicated and flawed characters and Will is one of those types that tugs at my emotions. This time around I got so frustrated with him and Angie, I wanted to throw the book across the room. Seriously, I had to take a break for a while and calm down. <br /><br />But the crime drama was absolutely insane! The last quarter of the book hits you with one Shockwave after another, leaving feeling almost weak with exhaustion. Good stuff! <br /><br />Overall, I’d say this book deserves the old five- star treatment. Can’t wait for the next book in the series! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2516030241640609414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399348556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9518734012292498129"><br/>I told myself I was going to write this review before starting <b>Broken</b> so here I am and I'm going to try and make it quick.<br/><br/><b>Undone</b> is my favorite so far of the <b>Will Trent Series</b> and I really should be taking the time to write a full review with perfect pictures but the next book is waiting on my Kindle! :)<br/><br/>For me this was the most gruesome of the three books. As with the others the writing was gripping and captivating. It created such vivid thoughts for me which at times had me squeezing my eyes sh</span>
  <span id="freeText9518734012292498129" style="display:none"><br>I told myself I was going to write this review before starting <b>Broken</b> so here I am and I'm going to try and make it quick.<br><br><b>Undone</b> is my favorite so far of the <b>Will Trent Series</b> and I really should be taking the time to write a full review with perfect pictures but the next book is waiting on my Kindle! :)<br><br>For me this was the most gruesome of the three books. As with the others the writing was gripping and captivating. It created such vivid thoughts for me which at times had me squeezing my eyes shut and chanting oh my god, oh my god… I guess I am a little twisted then to say that this is my favorite but it was. <br><br>The plot centers on women who share common threads. Someone believes they should be tormented and that they don’t belong. Some of the scenes are rather brutal and were difficult to read through. I had a constant feeling of dread. There are biblical references that make you stop and contemplate. I found myself completely immersed with Will and Faith as they set out to find this psycho.<br><br>I continue to appreciate the development of all the main characters as well as the introduction of new characters. In <b>Undone</b> we meet <b>Sara Linton.</b> I’m excited to find out where KS takes this character. She has some baggage she brings with her. Sadness and heartache that she desperately needs to let go of. I like her. <br><br><b>Amanda</b> continues to be a thorn in Will’s side. Quite honestly, this woman is ruthless and at times dispassionate. <b>Faith</b> really shined in this one. I love her "I don’t take shit from anyone" attitude. She wears it well. Her relationship with Will is starting to bloom both professionally and personally. She is good for him and that makes me happy. They haven’t crossed the romantic line and I don’t know if I would want them too. Time will tell I guess.<br><br>And <b>Will</b>. There are so many shades of this man. With every book there is a little more revealed. I feel happiness and sadness for him all at the same time. He has ability to make me laugh and in this one he had the ability to make me cry. There was a scene towards the end of the book that I sobbed through....<i>Will did not move for anything. He lay on the floor all night, until the sun coming through the windows told him it was time to go back to work.</i> I want him; no I need him to be happy. ❤<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445190115i/16612854.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Once again, I can’t end my review without a word or two about Angie. My hatred continues. I get it already. I understand their relationship but I want it to be over.<br><br>Moving on though and I’m off to read more of this <b>AMAZING</b> series!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9518734012292498129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3170921200" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6029173035708042934">4 Stars<br/><br/>A naked woman runs across a highway and is struck by a mobile home. Brought to Grady Hospital, she is attended to by Doctor Sara Linton who moved from Grant County to Atlanta four years ago. Will Trent and his partner Faith Mitchell of the GBI investigate as the bodies pile up.<br/><br/><u>A taut mystery/thriller that brings Will Trent and Sara Linton together. Hmm. Not sure how I feel about this </u> (though I already had an inkling having read “The Last Widow” before the entire Grant County series.. lol</span>
  <span id="freeText6029173035708042934" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />A naked woman runs across a highway and is struck by a mobile home. Brought to Grady Hospital, she is attended to by Doctor Sara Linton who moved from Grant County to Atlanta four years ago. Will Trent and his partner Faith Mitchell of the GBI investigate as the bodies pile up.<br /><br /><u>A taut mystery/thriller that brings Will Trent and Sara Linton together. Hmm. Not sure how I feel about this </u> (though I already had an inkling having read “The Last Widow” before the entire Grant County series.. lol!). Will Trent is a serious man and a loner. He’s never really let anyone in, not even his wife Angie with whom he has an on again off again relationship and who he has known since childhood. I want more for Will Trent - especially given the childhood he had and he definitely deserves more than Angie - that’s for sure, I just can’t say what that is. Sara Linton moved away from Grant County years ago to try and make a fresh start at Grady Hospital, back where it all started for her, in the ER. Sara hasn’t really had a life these last few years, yet that might be about to change. <b>Truthfully, I’m not sure I love this potential pairing and I am guessing that I’m totally alone here.. but my heart is still back in Grant County. </b> <br /><br /><b>I’ll tell you what I do like about this series: the pairing of Will Trent and Faith Mitchell as partners. Faith has spark! </b> I love how she trades barbs with Will and he is often left speechless. I just adore Faith’s character and can’t wait to see what’s in store for her. <br /><br />The mystery itself was full of twists and turns that really got me. The storyline almost made my heart stop near the end and there was a moment where I had to put the book down to catch my breath. <br /><br />Thank you to my local library for loaning me a copy of this audiobook.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads on 2.17.20.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9025102649048962057">4.5 "I fucking hate Angie" stars!<br/><br/>This series is a spin off from the Grant County series... I had started this series when I realised that one of the character who was going to show up in this series already featured in the other series... Now I am a bit of a stickler for reading in order, so I had to stop this series and go back to the other. Confused yet??<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442909894i/16293036.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Will and Faith work for the GBI (Georgia Bureau of Investigation). These two. Lord above, they sure have some baggage and interesting pasts, </span>
  <span id="freeText9025102649048962057" style="display:none">4.5 "I fucking hate Angie" stars!<br><br>This series is a spin off from the Grant County series... I had started this series when I realised that one of the character who was going to show up in this series already featured in the other series... Now I am a bit of a stickler for reading in order, so I had to stop this series and go back to the other. Confused yet??<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442909894i/16293036.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Will and Faith work for the GBI (Georgia Bureau of Investigation). These two. Lord above, they sure have some baggage and interesting pasts, especially Will. He is not even my typical hero/leading man but I do love him. I want to take care of him. I want him to have a lovely life... I want him to tell Angie to FUCK OFF.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Faith was not really his type but she was an attractive woman, and attractive women could get away with a lot. Sara Linton, for instance, could probably get away with murder.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>When I started this series, I wasn't sure how the romantic theme was going to go. I sort of wanted Will and Faith together but I think they are better as work partners ... but I want them to be friends. I want them to open up more to each other. Fingers crossed.<br><br><b>FAITH</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442909894i/16293037._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"She's not even a real doctor. She's a pediatrician.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Ouch, Faith, not nice ... she did her training as much as a "real" doctor.<br><br><b>SARA</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439226857i/15811070._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It was great to catch up with Sara. She has moved to Atlanta. Three years or more have passed since that harrowing event in her life. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"He's not crying. Why is he not crying?"</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442909894i/16293038._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Some of the scenes are fairly gruesome. Won't go into much detail. There are a lot of religious connotations also, which were interesting.<br><br>We have some side characters who appear throughout the books. Amanda. Jeez, she's a bit of a bitch. But I guess she didn't get that high up the ladder in what, in reality, is a "man's world."<br><br><br><b>AMANDA</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427587497i/14290413._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>He thought again about what Sara had said. Learn from your mistakes.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br> <b>ANGIE</b><br><br>No comment really about her. I think the author portrays her as a person we are not supposed to like. I certainly don't like her. But they have a history together.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442909894i/16293039.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>Will did not move for anything. He lay on the floor all night, until the sun coming through the windows told him it was time to go back to work.</b>

<div id="review_1683224144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1683224144" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1683224144?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1683224144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15504169900382475764">Will Trent and Sara Linton in the same book!!!!!!!! I can't read this fast enough. I loved the Grant County series. I could not read those books fast enough and I was so sad when that series ended with a BANG. But now I'm hooked with Will Trent and What! What! What! Sara Linton is in this book? Yes, Yes, and Yes!<br/><br/>A young woman enters the Trauma center where Sara now works. After her husbands death, Sara has left Grant County and now works at a hospital in Atlanta. She is on duty when the naked, t</span>
  <span id="freeText15504169900382475764" style="display:none">Will Trent and Sara Linton in the same book!!!!!!!! I can't read this fast enough. I loved the Grant County series. I could not read those books fast enough and I was so sad when that series ended with a BANG. But now I'm hooked with Will Trent and What! What! What! Sara Linton is in this book? Yes, Yes, and Yes!<br /><br />A young woman enters the Trauma center where Sara now works. After her husbands death, Sara has left Grant County and now works at a hospital in Atlanta. She is on duty when the naked, tortured woman is brought in for treatment. She literally shoves Will Tent out of the way in order to treat her patient. I loved this! Sara continues to be a strong female character.<br /><br />Will Trent is a the hospital with his partner Faith, when the tortured young woman is brought into he Emergency Room. He inserts himself in the investigation of what happened to this woman and bringing the perpetrator to justice. He treats the tortured woman with kindness and touches her foot tenderly which catches Sara's eye. He throws himself into the investigation and we get to see his brilliant mind at play. He continues to hide his dyslexia and fears it being found out by others. A little more is told about Will Trent. I have a feeling that with each book, a little more will be disclosed about him. Then there is his wife, Angie. I don't like her. I don't like her with Will. She is emotionally abusive. Why does he stay with her? Yes, they grew up in a group home together. Yes, she knows him better than anyone. But knowing someone and using their sad, horrible past as a way of hurting them does not for a healthy relationship make. <br /><br />Will Trent will not be the only character we learn more about, I have a feeling we will be seeing more of Faith in upcoming books. She is at the hospital receiving care (from Sara of course) and this opens up a story line for her as well. I like her attitude. We also get a little more of Amanda (Will's boos)in this one. Will is surrounded by strong women which makes his relationship with Angie so hard to swallow.<br /><br />The investigation of the tortured woman continues while another victim is quickly found by Will. Another woman goes missing and soon it appears that they missing women are similar in certain aspects. How do they all tie together? Who is taking them? What will happen next? Where will the beginning friendship with Sara take Will?<br /><br />Slaughter continues to dazzle with her character development. She continues to shine when writing carnage (is this a compliment) she does a good job giving us evil characters who do the unthinkable. She has a plot that is well thought out with twists and turns. This was a page turner for me!<br /><br />Keep em coming Slaughter. I have a feeling she is just getting warmed up with this series.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15504169900382475764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer529390065555709770"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442912798i/16293336._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well, I'm definitely whole-heartedly invested in this series now. And <b>Will Trent</b> has permanently gotten under my skin and into my heart. What can I say... Will, Will, Will. He is finally starting to break... to let some light into the cracks of that concrete wall he's erected around his heart. I've said it before and I'll say it again. it is impossible not to love this man. <br/><br/>This book has finally started giving me a little insight into the characters.. Will and his GBI partner <b>Faith Mitc</b></span>
  <span id="freeText529390065555709770" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442912798i/16293336._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, I'm definitely whole-heartedly invested in this series now. And <b>Will Trent</b> has permanently gotten under my skin and into my heart. What can I say... Will, Will, Will. He is finally starting to break... to let some light into the cracks of that concrete wall he's erected around his heart. I've said it before and I'll say it again. it is impossible not to love this man. <br><br>This book has finally started giving me a little insight into the characters.. Will and his GBI partner <b>Faith Mitchell</b> are finally starting to find a common ground as partners. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448117004i/17097497._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the more they get to know each other the closer they get. They fight like brother and sister, and yet there is this unspoken bond between them. Some secrets still remain between them, but they are slowly opening up to each other in ways that neither of them had expected. And there is now this spirit of over-protectiveness on both of their parts. For Will it relates to Faith's health issues, and for Faith it is Will's gentle and damaged soul, that until now has been his claim to fame. But it seems that the monster within is finally finding it's way to the surface. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"You're a good cop, Faith, and I'm glad you're my partner."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Faith is struggling with her personal life at the moment, and most of all some personal health issues that might affect her entire future. But still she carries on with her stressful job. She rarely lets her guard down, and I'm finding I really really like her. She is tough and funny as hell. And I love how she has taken Will under her wing, but not in a patronizing way, but instead in a caring and respectful way.<br><br>Then there is <b>Amanda Wagner</b>, <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448117004i/17097498.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>their ball-busting boss, who up until now I have really disliked. But, more and more as I learn about her history, and see her in action. I am really starting to love this character. But I must say, her motivations are still quite the mystery. And something about her harsh attitude towards Will, and now even his new partner, has me sensing a feeling of deep loyalty between them. <br><br>Now <b>Angie Polaski</b>,<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448117004i/17097499._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WIll's now <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[estranged wife <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, she is fucking up royally. And she is tormenting Will with the power she holds over him. I see bad things in her future. At least a girl can dream, right? <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Angie Polaski was looking like the biggest mistake Will had ever made in his miserable life.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Sara Linton, MD</b> is the new girl in town. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448117004i/17097500._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are still some secrets to come out about her past. I am looking forward to learning more about her story. And I'll thrilled that Will is finally starting to see the <i>normal</i> possibilities in a woman like Sara. And I think that she has more than noticed him. Can't wait to see where this relationship goes! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448117004i/17097501.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, the crimes in this book are gruesome as usual. I found it a touch more predictable that the last book, but in a good way. The story was more cohesive, and less erratic. Can't wait to jump into book 4! <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Considering what Pauline's been through..." Will began, then stopped himself. "She's not very nice."<br>"She's a cold-blooded bitch."<br>"I'm surprised I haven't fallen in love with her."<br>Faith laughed. She had seen Angie at the hospital when they brought Will out of surgery. "How is Mrs. Trent doing?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2306373326" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306373326" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306373326?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11520824-genesis">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306373326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17886433155820480119">I very much enjoyed this third thriller in Karin Slaughter's Will Trent series, although I'm wondering if I should have read her Grant County series first as a character with history in that series, Dr Sara Linton, has crossed over to this one in Atlanta. No problem so far but I suspect we're going to see more of her in future books. <br/><br/>This was a very suspenseful thriller opening with an elderly couple running into a naked woman running down the road. As well as being hit by their car, she is in a</span>
  <span id="freeText17886433155820480119" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed this third thriller in Karin Slaughter's Will Trent series, although I'm wondering if I should have read her Grant County series first as a character with history in that series, Dr Sara Linton, has crossed over to this one in Atlanta. No problem so far but I suspect we're going to see more of her in future books. <br /><br />This was a very suspenseful thriller opening with an elderly couple running into a naked woman running down the road. As well as being hit by their car, she is in a dreadful condition, after being starved, beaten and tortured in horrendous ways for several days. Special agents Will Trent and Faith Mitchell from the Georgia Bureau Investigation take over the case when they discover another victim and suspect that a recently abducted woman might also be about to undergo the same fate. It becomes a race against time to find the links between these women and the warped individual torturing them.<br /><br />Karin Slaughter's thrillers are always very character driven and the relationships between the characters are key to enjoying them. Will Trent is an abandoned child who grew up and suffered abuse in the State foster system. He is dyslexic and has trouble reading, although he was smart enough to get through high school and college and uses special software to help him at work. Faith, his partner, knows of his disability and as she values him highly as a smart and honest cop, helps to cover for him when required. Will and Faith's boss also knows about his reading difficulty but despite being cold and hard-nosed is prepared to overlook it for her best detective. This episode reveals that Faith is also likely to need some help and understanding from both Will and Amanda in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17886433155820480119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_398753322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/398753322" />
    <a title="Rick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8824769-rick"><img alt="Rick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360459107p2/8824769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/398753322?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick" href="/user/show/8824769-rick">Rick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398753322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1030003579640514869">I just discovered Karin Slaughter, and as most of you know, there's nothing as good as finding a "new" (to you) author who has many books already published. No "waiting for the next one to come out" anxiety!<br/>Before I had finished "Fractured" I KNEW I had to have "Undone"...and I wasn't disappointed. Slaughter came through for me again, with excellent suspense and a great cast of characters brought to life flawlessly and with depth.<br/><br/>Having never read the 'Grant County' series, I was afraid the rein</span>
  <span id="freeText1030003579640514869" style="display:none">I just discovered Karin Slaughter, and as most of you know, there's nothing as good as finding a "new" (to you) author who has many books already published. No "waiting for the next one to come out" anxiety!<br />Before I had finished "Fractured" I KNEW I had to have "Undone"...and I wasn't disappointed. Slaughter came through for me again, with excellent suspense and a great cast of characters brought to life flawlessly and with depth.<br /><br />Having never read the 'Grant County' series, I was afraid the reintroduction of Sara Linton would either confuse me (because I'd never heard of her) or mess up what I think is great chemistry between my favorite Georgia detectives Will Trent and Faith Mitchell. But the author works these three characters together seamlessly. *for more about these characters, please see my (or anyone's) reviews of earlier novels. It should also be noted that you need NOT know the backgrounds of these characters to enjoy this book. Yes, it is part of a series, but EACH BOOK STANDS ALONE JUST FINE!<br /><br />I've recommended "Undone" to friends, but always with a warning: this is a tale of a dark, violent, SERIOUSLY twisted sociopath and Ms. Slaughter doesn't pull her punches. The book doesn't include ACTS of torture or violence, but certainly &amp; thoroughly DESCRIBES the aftermath. The author's villain in this mystery/suspense novel is BEYOND demented and sadistic.<br /><br />Ms. Slaughter, I am learning, is an expert at leading her readers in so many directions--all connected, yet separate-- that during "Undone", at one time or another, I was SURE that everyone but the cops was the "guy who did it". And ya gotta love a crime novel that you can't figure out til the end! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1030003579640514869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9058958646413374046" style="display:none">Loving this series more with each book. I love Will, and I'm happy he's gaining some confidence and backbone. I think I dreaded the possibility of having a front row seat while the psycho was at work, and that didn't end up happening. <div id="review_997625407" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/997625407" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28831526-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579801852p2/28831526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/997625407?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/28831526-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997625407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12162011197396993895">If I hadn’t read Karin Slaughter previously, I might have been a bit put off just a few pages into the prologue of Undone. Having read quite a few of Slaughter’s previous thrillers, I was expecting something dramatic by, oh, the second paragraph. So I was almost lulled into complacency when it hit me – or rather, when Henry Coldfield and his wife Judith hit a woman as they drove at dusk one evening. Thus began the heart-pounding, stomach-churning tale that is Undone.<br/><br/>For those who have not finish</span>
  <span id="freeText12162011197396993895" style="display:none">If I hadn’t read Karin Slaughter previously, I might have been a bit put off just a few pages into the prologue of Undone. Having read quite a few of Slaughter’s previous thrillers, I was expecting something dramatic by, oh, the second paragraph. So I was almost lulled into complacency when it hit me – or rather, when Henry Coldfield and his wife Judith hit a woman as they drove at dusk one evening. Thus began the heart-pounding, stomach-churning tale that is Undone.<br /><br />For those who have not finished the Grant County series, this book may contain spoilers, because Ms. Slaughter brings back Dr. Sara Linton. It is over three years since her husband Jeffrey was killed, and Sara has moved to Atlanta to work in the ER at Grady Hospital, away from her parents and her practice, away from whatever might remind her of her late husband. Sara, who feels lost and must somehow find meaning in her life again.<br /><br />This book brings together Sara, Special Agent Will Trent, and Will’s partner Faith Mitchell. Each is flawed in his or her own way, and rather than judging their weaknesses, Ms. Slaughter seems to put the imperfections out there as if to say, “it is what it is; deal with it.” Somehow, each “weakness” becomes a strength, if not for that individual, then for the partner, as bonds are formed and strengthened. Call it forced compromise. Teamwork. Will is dyslexic. Faith learns that she is diabetic and pregnant. The two cops are polar opposites on the social skills scale, and each has problems there too. They have been partners for about a year at this point, and while they still drive each other crazy sometimes, at this point they seem to have an alliance that works well for them more often than not. It is the first time that Will and Faith meet Sara Linton, and this evokes some conflicting emotions for all as the story moves along.<br /><br />The two Special Agents and Dr. Linton meet at the ER. The woman who was hit by the car turns out to have escaped from a psychopathic kidnapper who tortured her and another woman in horrendous ways. We don’t read these events as they occur, thankfully; just having them revealed after the fact is upsetting enough. The hunt for clues and suspects begins. There may be more victims. <br /><br />I had a good idea who the perpetrator was early on, but the story was more complex, of course, than what I could imagine. In true Slaughter fashion, there are moral questions to be faced – by the killer’s family, by Will, by Faith, and even by the victims. There’s no happy-ever-after ending either, even after the bad guy is caught. As always, scars remain, inside and out.<br /><br />5 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12162011197396993895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15031636139757807156" style="display:none">Another good addition in the Will Trent series and by far the most gruesome in the series so far. Will and Faith are after a killer who kidnaps two victims at a time and keeps them under the ground in a hand made cave. The women endure horrible tortures, definitely not for the faint of heart. Faith has some health complications which lead her to Sarah, an ER doctor who is a character that comes from Karin Slaughters other series, Grant County. Sarah is known in the medical community for her knowledge in forensic science and is a nice addition to the series, however, she is a complicated and injured soul. A surprising twist at the end is frightening and especially dangerous for Will and Faith. All the usual characters are back and of course complicating Will's life. </span>

<div id="review_1419116488" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419116488" />
    <a title="Piper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10095424-piper"><img alt="Piper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571200889p2/10095424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419116488?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piper" href="/user/show/10095424-piper">Piper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10095424-piper?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419116488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9850031356183052352">Another great Will Trent installment from Karin Slaughter, <b>Undone</b> certainly had me shuddering at times from the hideously gruesome things that were done to the female victims. These women already had deep seated issues but to be violated as they were was inconceivable. The perp was undeniably a sick SOB. What was almost even sicker was who knew what he was doing and kept silent about it. Yeah. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447742943i/17045458._SX540_.jpg' width='400”' height='241"<br' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What I love about this series, first and foremost, is Will Trent. He is, as others have stated before, </span>
  <span id="freeText9850031356183052352" style="display:none">Another great Will Trent installment from Karin Slaughter, <b>Undone</b> certainly had me shuddering at times from the hideously gruesome things that were done to the female victims. These women already had deep seated issues but to be violated as they were was inconceivable. The perp was undeniably a sick SOB. What was almost even sicker was who knew what he was doing and kept silent about it. Yeah. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447742943i/17045458._SX540_.jpg" width="400”" height='241"&lt;br' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I love about this series, first and foremost, is Will Trent. He is, as others have stated before, an enigma. He is sexy in his own right, yet so flawed that he cannot see his way around it. I want more than anything for him to find and know true happiness.<br>There were more sides of him revealed in this novel, yet I feel there is much more of him to be discovered. At least I hope so. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447742964i/17045459._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="460”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reappearing characters are Faith Mitchell, Will’s partner, Amanda Wagner, Will’s boss, and Angie. <br><br>Faith has to deal with some personal issues in this story, but she is one tough gal, and I have no doubt she will overcome them. While she and Will are still struggling a bit in their communication skills with one another, they are making headway. I like Faith- she has a good heart. <br><br>Amanda is a tough bitch, but she also takes care of her own when the need arises. It’s suggested that she had to be tough to get where she is, and I’ve no doubt that it’s the truth. <br><br><b>”Glad to see you finally grow a pair,” Amanda told Will. “You’re suspended without pay for the rest of the week, but don’t think for a damn minute that means you’re going to stop working your ass off for me.”</b><br><br>Now Angie- she is just your basic, manipulative bitch. I gave her the benefit of the doubt in the first book, but not anymore. She does not play fair and I’m getting really tired of her shit. Someone needs to teach her a lesson in goodbye. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447743004i/17045460._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="600”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, we are introduced to Dr. Sara Linton in this third book. She also has a past that haunts her. She wants to be released from it- to move forward, but doesn’t seem to know how to do that. I very much hope that she finds a way.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447743004i/17045461._SY540_.jpg" width="400”" height="533”&lt;br" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lastly, there was one scene in this story that ripped my heart out. I don’t want to give anything away, but the character that was portrayed in both Will and Faith when it happened really moved me. There were others parts as well that were tough to take. This was just as much an emotional story as it was gruesome, really. I highly recommend it to anyone who enjoys the crime/suspense genre. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9850031356183052352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2375133327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2375133327" />
    <a title="Hollis " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16668577-hollis"><img alt="Hollis " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586714618p2/16668577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2375133327?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollis " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollis " href="/user/show/16668577-hollis">Hollis </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440244455" href="/book/show/7573275-undone">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Hollis  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11622887-paula">Paula</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=book-buddy-recs">book-buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=buddy-read-sorta">buddy-read-sorta</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=heroes-to-root-for">heroes-to-root-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=sexytimes">sexytimes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2375133327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1059377979126159695">Okay. Okay. I'm starting to see it now. I don't want to get too excited and set myself up for possibly being blindsided by future irritations with this main character, but I definitely think book two's mystery coloured my feelings for Will. It was all around a really hashed up job and that rubbed off not only on the characters but on me as a reader. <br/><br/>While in UNDONE all the victims are almost as equally unpleasant as the villain (on the one hand, it's awesome that you can't feel total sympathy fo</span>
  <span id="freeText1059377979126159695" style="display:none">Okay. Okay. I'm starting to see it now. I don't want to get too excited and set myself up for possibly being blindsided by future irritations with this main character, but I definitely think book two's mystery coloured my feelings for Will. It was all around a really hashed up job and that rubbed off not only on the characters but on me as a reader. <br /><br />While in UNDONE all the victims are almost as equally unpleasant as the villain (on the one hand, it's awesome that you can't feel total sympathy for them because that's such a change, but on the other, jfc, Slaughter, give me <b>someone</b> to care about), and though Faith's bitchiness was somewhat due to health factors, Will was the shining star here. And oddly he was far from perfect, did a few questionable and seemingly out of character things, but nonetheless.. it worked. From an author who seems to thrive on creating unlikeable characters that I hate, she made the likeable one show signs of awfulness and created a dialogue surrounding the behaviour of doing wrong. And making sure not to repeat it. I loved it. So, yes, shining star. But he wasn't the only one. <br /><br />We had a blast from the <i>Grant County</i> past that I have long been expecting and.. wow. I hate to say it but I like her better now than I ever have before. I thought the introduction of this character, the tie-in to the other series, and the explanation of what has happened in the years since, so emotional. And I'm so hopeful for.. things. Even if Angie is still fucking things up and making those things seem unlikely. Also shoutout to Amanda for being stone cold ruthless and complete #bitchgoals.<br /><br />Really excited about this binge now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1059377979126159695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12640016102209072382">Great book. I could not stop reading it. Karin Slaughter in one of my favorite authors and I've read many of her books. But I decided to go back and read some in the series that I had missed. She has two main characters in her books - Will and Sara. Will is a GBI agent and Sarah is a doctor. This is the book where they met and the next book in the series would be where their relationship started. I love these books and one of the reasons is that I have live in the Atlanta, GA metro area most of </span>
  <span id="freeText12640016102209072382" style="display:none">Great book. I could not stop reading it. Karin Slaughter in one of my favorite authors and I've read many of her books. But I decided to go back and read some in the series that I had missed. She has two main characters in her books - Will and Sara. Will is a GBI agent and Sarah is a doctor. This is the book where they met and the next book in the series would be where their relationship started. I love these books and one of the reasons is that I have live in the Atlanta, GA metro area most of my life and I love reading about locations that I am familiar with. Look forward to my next book by this author.</span>

<div id="review_851383242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851383242" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7291253-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350595639p2/7291253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/851383242?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7291253-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer851383242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15617407682420348021">2nd read - Great Slaughter read, such as Will's assessment of his boss, Amanda: "Will heard leaves rustling, branches snapping. He turned to find Amanda Wagner making her way through the woods. She was an older woman, probably in her sixties. She favored monochromatic power suits that hit below her knee and stockings that showed off the definition of what Will had to admit were remarkably good calves for a woman he often thought of as the Antichrist."<br/><br/>Will's taken over a case from another county,</span>
  <span id="freeText15617407682420348021" style="display:none">2nd read - Great Slaughter read, such as Will's assessment of his boss, Amanda: "Will heard leaves rustling, branches snapping. He turned to find Amanda Wagner making her way through the woods. She was an older woman, probably in her sixties. She favored monochromatic power suits that hit below her knee and stockings that showed off the definition of what Will had to admit were remarkably good calves for a woman he often thought of as the Antichrist."<br /><br />Will's taken over a case from another county, and no one there appreciates it. Someone has kidnapped a pair of women and tortured them before the ladies escaped. Unless Will and his partner Faith can solve the case, it will happen again. Throw in Faith's secret pregnancy and hidden diabetes, she bites Will's head off every other minute. <br /> <br />We get to witness Will's first meeting of Sarah, a character from Slaughter's excellent Grant County series, and the sparks get ready to fly, just as Will's estranged wife, psycho Angie, comes back into the picture.<br /><br />1st read - This is the 3rd Will Trent book and the best so far. His partner is pregnant, Angie has been gone several months and he insinuates himself into another jurisdiction's case. A naked woman has been hit by a car and on arrival at the hospital, it's found she's been tortured. A new character, the physician Sara, is introduced, although she's been in another series, Grant County. I really enjoy Slaughter's writing style and look forward to the Grant Co. stories.</span>

    <a title="Jonetta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta"><img alt="Jonetta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329083158p2/4876540.jpg" /></a>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423342311" href="/book/show/6821293-undone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569205116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2993576286944824575">It's been over three years since Sara Linton left Grant County following her personal tragedy and she's now working in Atlanta, back at Grady Hospital. Though she's moving forward with her life, it's still a slow pace. When she attends a woman who shows up in the ER, obviously brutalized, Sara is hurtled into an investigation that leads to more horror and Will Trent (he's not the horror!). <br/><br/>This marks the intersection of the Grant County series and I was glad to see Sara reappear here. She and Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText2993576286944824575" style="display:none">It's been over three years since Sara Linton left Grant County following her personal tragedy and she's now working in Atlanta, back at Grady Hospital. Though she's moving forward with her life, it's still a slow pace. When she attends a woman who shows up in the ER, obviously brutalized, Sara is hurtled into an investigation that leads to more horror and Will Trent (he's not the horror!). <br /><br />This marks the intersection of the Grant County series and I was glad to see Sara reappear here. She and Will have an obvious connection, though not necessarily a romantic one yet. Their contributions to the investigation fit nicely and I liked the direction. <br /><br />Speaking of the case, this was a real puzzler and the lines between victims and perpetrators weren't always clear. It just made things that more interesting and maddening. I'm not sure what to make of it all but there was a lot I liked about the journey to the end. As always, the narration was excellent, drawing clear character distinctions and augmenting the story without overwhelming the narrative. I can't seem to get enough of this series, despite the occasional gruesome passage. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2993576286944824575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
